       <h1>Key Concepts</h1> 
       <div class="row section"> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12"> 
         <h2 id="Getting-Started"> Getting Started <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/01 Key Concepts/01 Getting Started" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true" style="font-size:0.7em;"></i> </a> <a href="#Getting-Started" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h2> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container"></div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Getting-Started-Welcome"> Welcome <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/01 Key Concepts/01 Getting Started/01 Welcome" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Getting-Started-Welcome" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <meta name="tag" content="using quantconnect"> 
          <p> <b>Welcome to QuantConnect.</b> We are an open source, community driven algorithmic trading platform. Our trading engine is powered by <a href="https://lean.quantconnect.com" target="_BLANK">LEAN</a>, a cross platform, multi-asset technology which brings cutting edge finance to the open source community. We support <b>C#</b>, <b>Python</b> and <b>F#</b> programming languages making us a truly open platform. </p> 
          <h3> Our Mission </h3> 
          <p> We believe the future of finance is automated and we plan to be the quantitative trading infrastructure of the future. We believe algorithmic trading is a powerful tool and we want to open it up to all investors. </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill">

         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Getting-Started-Security--Privacy"> Security Privacy <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/01 Key Concepts/01 Getting Started/02 Security  Privacy" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Getting-Started-Security--Privacy" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <meta name="tag" content="using quantconnect"> 
          <p> You own all your intellectual property and your code. Your code is private by default unless you explicitly share it with the community in the forums or with another team member via collaboration. You are creating valuable intellectual property and we respect this, and wish to make it easier.Only two QuantConnect staff members have access to the database. If we ever need access to your algorithm for the purpose of debugging, we only explicitly request permission first. Please see our <a href="/terms" target="_BLANK">terms and conditions</a>. </p>

          <h3 id="Getting-Started-Business-Model"> Business Model <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/01 Key Concepts/01 Getting Started/04 Business Model" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Getting-Started-Business-Model" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <meta name="tag" content="using quantconnect"> 
          <p> QuantConnect makes backtesting available for free and charges a small monthly fee to cover live algorithm trading. This offsets our costs and aligns our interests with yours - our client. We also work with brokerages to make your live trading free. </p>

         <h2 id="Developing-in-the-IDE"> Developing in the IDE <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/01 Key Concepts/02 Developing in the IDE" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true" style="font-size:0.7em;"></i> </a> <a href="#Developing-in-the-IDE" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h2> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container"></div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Developing-in-the-IDE-Coding-Your-Algorithm"> Coding Your Algorithm <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/01 Key Concepts/02 Developing in the IDE/01 Coding Your Algorithm" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Developing-in-the-IDE-Coding-Your-Algorithm" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <meta name="tag" content="using quantconnect"> 
          <p> Write code in project files and then press the <i class="fa fa-cogs"></i> Build button to compile your algorithm. Build errors will be displayed in the console and highlighted with red-lines. </p> 
          <p> You can add, rename and delete files in your project in the Projects tab. You can create a virtual folder for your project by placing a slash ("/") into the name of your file. </p> 
          <p> </p>
          <div class="copy-snippet nocopy"> 
           <p> Algorithms require only initialization and data event handlers. </p> 
           <pre class="prettyprint">public class BasicTemplateAlgorithm : QCAlgorithm
{
	public override void Initialize() {
		// Setup algorithm requirements: cash, dates and securities.
                // Initialize is called once at the start of the algorithm.
	}

	public override void OnData(Slice data) {
               // Data requested is then piped into event handlers like this one.
	}
}
</pre> 
          </div> 
          <p></p> 
         </div> 
        </div>

           <figcaption>
             QuantConnect Backtesting and Coding Environment.

          <h3 id="Developing-in-the-IDE-Backtesting-Your-Algorithm"> Backtesting Your Algorithm <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/01 Key Concepts/02 Developing in the IDE/02 Backtesting Your Algorithm" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Developing-in-the-IDE-Backtesting-Your-Algorithm" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <meta name="tag" content="using quantconnect"> 
          <p> Once you've got an algorithm compiling you can click the <i class="fa fa-play"></i> Play button to launch a backtest. You can launch as many backtests as want in parallel and results are shown in the result drop-down. </p> 
         </div>

          <meta name="tag" content="using quantconnect">

          <h3 id="Developing-in-the-IDE-Data-Manager"> Data Manager <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/01 Key Concepts/02 Developing in the IDE/04 Data Manager" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Developing-in-the-IDE-Data-Manager" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <meta name="tag" content="using quantconnect">

       <h1>Algorithm Reference</h1> 
       <div class="row section"> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12"> 
         <h2 id="Overview"> Overview <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/01 Overview" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true" style="font-size:0.7em;"></i> </a> <a href="#Overview" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h2> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container"></div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style="border-bottom: 1px solid #eee; "> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Overview-Overview"> <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/01 Overview/01 Overview" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Overview-Overview" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <meta name="tag" content="using quantconnect"> 
          <p> QuantConnect's LEAN engine manages your portfolio and data feeds letting you focus on your algorithm strategy and execution. Data is piped into your strategy via event handlers, upon which you can place trades. We provide basic portfolio management and fill modelling underneath the hood automatically. This is provided by the <code>QCAlgorithm</code> base class. </p> 
          <p> All algorithms extend <code>QCAlgorithm</code>, which provides some key helper properties for you to use: Security Manager, Portfolio Manager, Transactions Manager, Notification Manager and Scheduling Manager. Along with hundreds of helper methods to make the API easy to use. We'll go into more detail on those below, but its important for you to know the basic infrastructure around your algorithm. </p> 
          <p> The <code class="csharp visualbasic fsharp python">Securities</code> <span class="csharp visualbasic fsharp python">property</span><code class="java">get_Securities()</code> <span class="java">method</span> is a dictionary of Security objects. Each asset (equity, forex pair etc) in your algorithm has a security object. All the models for a security live on these objects: e.g. <span class="csharp visualbasic fsharp python"><code>Securities["IBM"].FeeModel</code> or <code>Securities["IBM"].Price</code>.</span><code class="java">get_Securities().get_Item("SPY").get_Price()</code> </p> 
          <p> <code>Portfolio</code> is a dictionary of SecurityHolding classes. These classes track the individual portfolio items profit and losses, fees and quantity held. e.g. <code class="csharp visualbasic fsharp python">Portfolio["IBM"].LastTradeProfit</code><code class="java">Decimal profit = get_Portfolio().get_Item("IBM").get_LastTradeProfit();</code>. </p> 
          <p> Other helpers like <code>Transactions</code>, <code>Schedule</code>, <code>Notify</code>, and <code>Universe</code> have their own helper methods which we'll explain below. </p> 
          <p> All algorithms must have an <code>Initialize()</code> method to setup your strategy. Once setup most algorithms have OnData event handlers to process market data and make trading decisions. </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example all"> 
          <pre>public class QCAlgorithm
{
        SecurityManager Securities;   //Array of Security objects.
        SecurityPortfolioManager Portfolio;  // Array of SecurityHolding objects
        SecurityTransactionManager Transactions;  // Transactions helper
        ScheduleManager Schedule;  // Scheduling helper
        NotificationManager Notify; //Email, SMS helper
        UniverseManager Universe; // Universe helper
 
        //Set up Requested Data, Cash, Time Period.
        public virtual void Initialize() { ... };
 
        //Event Handlers:
        public virtual OnData(Slice data) { ... };
        public virtual OnDividend() { ... };
        public virtual OnEndOfDay() { ... };
        public virtual OnEndOfAlgorithm() { ... };
        
        //Helpers... 
        public SimpleMovingAverage SMA();
}</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section"> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12"> 
         <h2 id="Initializing-Algorithms"> Initializing Algorithms <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/02 Initializing Algorithms" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true" style="font-size:0.7em;"></i> </a> <a href="#Initializing-Algorithms" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h2> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container"></div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Initializing-Algorithms-Initializing-Algorithms"> <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/02 Initializing Algorithms/01 Initializing Algorithms" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Initializing-Algorithms-Initializing-Algorithms" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <meta name="tag" content="using quantconnect"> 
          <p> The Initialize method is called to setup your strategy. Here you can request data, set starting cash or warm up periods. </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Initializing-Algorithms-Setting-Cash"> Setting Cash <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/02 Initializing Algorithms/02 Setting Cash" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Initializing-Algorithms-Setting-Cash" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <meta name="tag" content="securities and portfolio"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="portfolio setup"> 
          <p> In backtests you can set your starting capital using the <code class="csharp visualbasic java">SetCash(decimal cash)</code><code class="python">self.SetCash(decimal cash)</code><code class="fsharp">this.SetCash(decimal cash)</code> method. In live trading this is ignored and your brokerage cash is used instead. In paper trading we set the cash to a fictional $100,000 USD (you can override the paper trading equity by clicking the "Live Algorithm Equity" button in your project tab). </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">SetCash(25000);</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example fsharp"> 
          <pre class="fsharp">this.SetCash(100000)</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python">self.SetCash(100000)</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Initializing-Algorithms-Setting-Dates"> Setting Dates <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/02 Initializing Algorithms/03 Setting Dates" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Initializing-Algorithms-Setting-Dates" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <p> Backtesting uses the <code class="csharp java visualbasic">SetStartDate(int year, int month, int day)</code> <code class="python">self.SetStartDate(int year, int month, int day)</code> <code class="fsharp">this.SetStartDate(int year, int month, int day)</code> and <code class="csharp java visualbasic">SetEndDate(int year, int month, int day)</code> <code class="python">self.SetEndDate(int year, int month, int day)</code> <code class="fsharp">this.SetEndDate(int year, int month, int day)</code> methods to configure the backtest time range. If unspecified the end date defaults to yesterday. <span class="csharp visualbasic fsharp">In .NET languages you can also use a DateTime object to set the dates.</span> </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">SetStartDate(2013, 1, 1);         // Set start date to specific date.
SetEndDate(2015, 1, 1);         // Set end date to specific date.
SetEndDate(DateTime.Now.Date.AddDays(-1)); // Or use a relative date.</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python">self.SetStartDate(2013,1,1)
self.SetEndDate(2015,1,1)
self.SetEndDate(datetime.now() - timedelta(1)) # Or use a relative date.</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example fsharp"> 
          <pre class="fsharp">this.SetStartDate(2013, 10, 7)
this.SetEndDate(2013, 10, 11)</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Initializing-Algorithms-Selecting-Asset-Data"> Selecting Asset Data <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/02 Initializing Algorithms/04 Selecting Asset Data" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Initializing-Algorithms-Selecting-Asset-Data" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <meta name="tag" content="universes"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="custom universes"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="using data"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="assets"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="equity"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="adjusted pricing"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="forex"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="cfd"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="options"> 
          <p> Algorithms can manually subscribe to data for specific assets they need, or use universes to choose groups of assets based on filtering criteria (e.g. all stocks with volumes greater than $10M/day). See more about Universes <a href="#Universes">here</a>. </p> 
          <p> To manually subscribe to a specific asset you can call the <code>AddEquity()</code>, <code>AddForex()</code>, <code>AddCfd()</code> and <code>AddOption()</code> methods in your Initialize() method. You can subscribe to 500 minute resolution datafeeds, 100 second resolutions feeds and 10 tick resolution datafeeds. </p> 
          <p> QuantConnect supports international trading across multiple timezones and markets. Markets are used to distinguish between the same tickers on different exchanges (e.g. FXCM and OANDA both offer EURUSD, but have different rates). </p> 
          <p> QuantConnect provides 40TB of US Equities, US Options, FXCM FX and OANDA FX data. Check out more information about our data in our <a href="/data">data library</a>. </p> 
          <p> We provide data in tick, second, minute, hour or daily resolutions. These are specified by the <code>Resolution</code> enum. </p> 
          <p> If there is a gap in the data (e.g. because there are no trades), by default the data is still pumped into your strategy on each time step. This behavior is called "fillForward" and defaults to true. You can disable this by setting fillForward to false. </p> 
          <p> By default equity data in QuantConnect is Split and Dividend adjusted backwards in time to give smooth continuous prices. This allows easy use for indicators. Some algorithms need raw or partially adjusted price data. You can control this with the <code>SetDataNormalizationMode()</code> method. The <code>DataNormalizationMode</code> enum has the values Adjusted (default), Raw, SplitAdjusted, and TotalReturn. When data is set to Raw mode the dividends are paid as cash into your algorithm and the splits are directly applied to your holding quantity. </p> 
          <p> If you have your own custom data you'd like to backtest against, check out the <a href="#Custom-Data">custom data</a> section. </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example all"> 
          <pre>// Complete Add Equity API - Including Default Parameters:
AddEquity(string ticker, Resolution resolution = Resolution.Minute, string market = Market.USA, bool fillDataForward = true, decimal leverage = 0m, bool extendedMarketHours = false)

//Complete Add Forex API - Including Default Parameters:
AddForex(string ticker, Resolution resolution = Resolution.Minute, string market = Market.FXCM, bool fillDataForward = true, decimal leverage = 0m)</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">AddEquity("AAPL"); //Add Apple 1 minute bars (minute by default).
AddForex("EURUSD", Resolution.Second); //Add EURUSD 1 second bars.</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example fsharp"> 
          <pre class="fsharp">this.AddEquity("SPY", Resolution.Minute) |&gt; ignore
this.AddForex("EURUSD", Resolution.Second) |&gt; ignore</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python">self.AddEquity("SPY")  # Default to minute bars
self.AddForex("EURUSD", Resolution.Second) # Set second bars.</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">//Setting the data normalization mode for the MSFT security to raw (pay dividends as cash)
Securities["MSFT"].SetDataNormalizationMode(DataNormalizationMode.Raw);</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python"># Setting the data normalization mode for the MSFT security to raw (pay dividends as cash)
self.Securities["SPY"].SetDataNormalizationMode(DataNormalizationMode.Raw);</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example fsharp"> 
          <pre class="fsharp">(* Setting MSFT security to use raw prices *)
this.Securities.Item("MSFT").SetDataNormalizationMode(DataNormalizationMode.Raw);</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Initializing-Algorithms-Setting-Warm-Up-Period"> Setting Warm Up Period <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/02 Initializing Algorithms/05 Setting Warm Up Period" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Initializing-Algorithms-Setting-Warm-Up-Period" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <meta name="tag" content="history amd warm up"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="history"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="warm up"> 
          <p> Often algorithms need some historical data to prime technical indicators, or populate historical data arrays. Using the <code>SetWarmUp(TimeSpan period)</code> or <code>SetWarmUp(int barCount)</code> methods you can specify a warm up period for your algorithm which pumps data in from before the start date. During the warm up period you cannot place a trade. </p> 
          <p> Algorithms can use the <code>bool IsWarmingUp</code> property to determine if the warm up period has completed. </p> 
          <p> See more about using historical data in the <a href="#Historical-Data">History</a> section. </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">SetWarmUp(200); //Warm up 200 bars for all subscribed data.
SetWarmUp(TimeSpan.FromDays(7)); //Warm up 7 days of data.</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python">self.SetWarmUp(200) //Warm up 200 bars for all subscribed data.
self.SetWarmUp(timedelta(7)) //Warm up 7 days of data.</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example fsharp"> 
          <pre class="fsharp">this.SetWarmUp(200)</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style="border-bottom: 1px solid #eee; "> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Initializing-Algorithms-Cash-and-Brokerage-Models"> Cash and Brokerage Models <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/02 Initializing Algorithms/06 Cash and Brokerage Models" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Initializing-Algorithms-Cash-and-Brokerage-Models" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <meta name="tag" content="brokerage models"> 
          <p> US Equity brokerage accounts are either Cash or Margin based accounts. Cash accounts do not allow leveraged trading, whereas Margin accounts support 2-4x leverage on your account value. You can set your brokerage account type in your initialization with <code>SetBrokerageModel(BrokerageName broker, AccountType account);</code>. </p> 
          <p> The <code>BrokerageName</code> enum supports values of Default, TradierBrokerage, InteractiveBrokersBrokerage, FxcmBrokerage and OandaBrokerage. When setting the brokerage name we also set the trading fee structures for that brokerage. </p> 
          <p> The <code>AccountType</code> enum supports values of Cash and Margin. When using cash leverage is disabled by default, and the cash settlement period is set to 3 days. Margin accounts are settled immediately and have a leverage of 2. </p> 
          <p> Margin accounts with more than $25,000 in equity are eligible for pattern day trading margin limits. This increases your available leverage to 4x while the market is open and 2x overnight. To model this behavior in your algorithm you must set your security <code>MarginModel</code> a <code>PatternDayTradingMarginModel</code> class. </p> 
          <p> See more about brokerage models in the <a href="#Reality-Modelling">Reality Modelling</a> section. </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">//Brokerage model and account type:
SetBrokerageModel(BrokerageName.InteractiveBrokersBrokerage, AccountType.Margin);

//Add securities and if required set custom margin models 
var spy = AddEquity("SPY"); //Defaults to minute bars.
spy.MarginModel = new PatternDayTradingMarginModel();
</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python">#Brokerage model and account type:
self.SetBrokerageModel(BrokerageName.InteractiveBrokersBrokerage, AccountType.Cash)

//Add securities and if required set custom margin models 
spy = self.AddEquity("SPY") # Default to minute bars
spy.MarginModel = PatternDayTradingMarginModel()
</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example fsharp"> 
          <pre class="fsharp">(* In Initialize method, set the brokerage models *)
this.SetBrokerageModel(BrokerageName.InteractiveBrokersBrokerage, AccountType.Cash);
this.AddEquity("SPY", Resolution.Second) |&gt; ignore
(* Then if required, you can set specific margin models for your secutities *)
this.Securities.Item("SPY").MarginModel &lt;- new PatternDayTradingMarginModel()</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">// You can also create your own brokerage model: IBrokerageModel
class MyBrokerage: DefaultBrokerage {
   // Custom implementation of brokerage here.
} 

SetBrokerageModel(new MyBrokerage());</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section"> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12"> 
         <h2 id="Handling-Data"> Handling Data <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/03 Handling Data" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true" style="font-size:0.7em;"></i> </a> <a href="#Handling-Data" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h2> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container"></div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Handling-Data-Handling-Data"> <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/03 Handling Data/01 Handling Data" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Handling-Data-Handling-Data" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <meta name="tag" content="data event handlers"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="tradebars event"> 
          <p> Requested data is passed into event handlers for you to use to make trading decisions. The primary event handler, Slice, groups all data types together at a single moment in time in the <code>OnData(Slice data)</code> handler. Slice is short for "time slice" - representing a slice of time and values of the data at that time. <span class="csharp fsharp"> C# and F# also allow you to receive data with dedicated event handlers for each data type e.g <code>OnData(TradeBars data)</code>.</span><span class="python">Python only supports the Slice event handlers.</span> </p> 
          <p> All data uses <code>DataDictionary</code> objects to group data by symbol and provide easy access to information. The plural of the type denotes the collection of objects e.g. the <i>TradeBars</i> DataDictionary is made up of <i>TradeBar</i> objects. You can access individual data points in the dictionary through its string or symbol dictionary index. For example <code>var ibmTradeBar = tradebars["IBM"]</code>. </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Handling-Data-Time-Slices"> Time Slices <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/03 Handling Data/02 Time Slices" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Handling-Data-Time-Slices" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <meta name="tag" content="data event handlers"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="options"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="futures"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="tradebars event"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="ticks event"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="splits event"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="dividends event"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="delistings event"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="symbol changed event"> 
          <p> The Slice event handler combine all of the data together into a single method. It represents the data at a point in time. The <code>Slice</code> object contains many helpers for accessing your data. The Slice objects arrive to the <code>OnData(Slice data)</code> event handler. </p> 
          <p> The <code>Slice</code> object gives you three ways to access your data: </p> 
          <ol> 
           <li> Dynamic string/symbol indexer which returns a dynamic object of your type slice["IBM"]. </li> 
           <li> Statically typed properties (slice.Bars[], slice.QuoteBars[]). </li> 
           <li> Statically typed Get&lt;T&gt;() helper </li> 
          </ol> 
          <p> Strongly typed access gives you compile time safety but dynamic types can sometimes simplify coding. We recommend static types as they are easier to debug. </p> 
          <p> <span class="python">Python is dynamically typed so does not have the Get method. Primary Slice data access is through the string/symbol indexer.</span> </p> 
          <p> <span class="csharp fsharp visualbasic">Slice is the recommended method for data access in your algorithm.</span> </p> 
          <p> Slice has the following internal structure: </p> 
          <pre>class Slice : IEnumerable&lt;KeyValuePair&lt;Symbol, BaseData&gt;&gt;
{
    TradeBars Bars;
    QuoteBars QuoteBars;
    Ticks Ticks;
    OptionChains OptionChains;
    FuturesChains FuturesChains;
    Splits Splits;
    Dividends Dividends;
    Delistings Delistings;
    SymbolChangedEvents SymbolChangedEvents;
}</pre> 
          <p> It contains all the data for a given moment of time. TradeBars and QuoteBars are symbol/string indexed dictionaries so you can easily access the data. Ticks is a symbol-list dictionary with a list of ticks for that moment of time. </p> 
          <p> To make accessing the data easier the Slice object itself can also be indexed. e.g. <code>slice["IBM"]</code> will return a <b>TradeBar</b> for IBM. <code>slice["EURUSD"]</code> will return a <b>QuoteBar</b> for EURUSD. </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">// Event handler for Slice method
public void OnData(Slice data) {
}</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example fsharp"> 
          <pre class="fsharp">// Event handler for Slice method
member this.OnData(slice:Slice) =  
      ()</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python"># Event handler for the slice method
def OnData(self, slice):
    pass</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">//Access data in a Slice object: 
// 1. Strong Typed Properties: Ticks, TradeBars, Delistings, SymbolChangedEvents, Splits and Dividends
var bars = slice.Bars; // e.g. bars["IBM"].Open

// 2. Strong Typed Get Accessor:
var bars = slice.Get&lt;TradeBars&gt;(); //e.g. bars["IBM"].Open
var bar   = slice.Get&lt;TradeBar&gt;("IBM"); //e.g. bar.Open

// 3. Dynamic String / Symbol Indexer:
var bar = slice["IBM"]; // e.g. bar.Open</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python">#Access data in a Slice object: 
# 1. Grouped Properties: Ticks, Bars, Delistings, SymbolChangedEvents, Splits and Dividends
bars = slice.Bars; # e.g. bars["IBM"].Open

# 2. Dynamic String / Symbol Indexer:
bar = slice["IBM"] # e.g. bar.Open - TradeBar properties OHLCV
spyTickList = data["SPY"] # Tick assets return a list of Tick objects.</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Handling-Data-Event-Handlers"> Event Handlers <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/03 Handling Data/03 Event Handlers" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Handling-Data-Event-Handlers" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <meta name="tag" content="data event handlers"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="live trading"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="ticks event"> 
          <p> <span class="csharp fsharp"> In C#/F# data is also piped into dedicated event handlers for each data type. To use data this way you need to put an event handler in your algorithm which follows the pattern: <code> public void OnData(TradeBars data) {}</code>. LEAN automatically detects the method exists and sends data to it. </span> <span class="python"> Python does not support dedicated event data handlers. Slice is the preferred way to access data for your strategy. </span> </p> 
          <p> When working with Ticks they can occur at the same moment of time across different exchanges. Because of this we provide the ticks as a list. In backtesting this moment is stepped each second and you will get many ticks per second; in live trading it is stepped as fast as possible and you will probably get 1 tick per event. <span class="csharp"> The <code>public void OnData(Ticks data) {}</code> event handler captures these events. </span> To understand the event handlers you should click on each class object link below to see its structure. </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">public void OnData(TradeBars data) {
    // TradeBars objects are piped into this method.
}
public void OnData(Ticks data) {
    // Ticks objects are piped into this method.
}</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style="border-bottom: 1px solid #eee; "> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Handling-Data-Data-Formats"> Data Formats <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/03 Handling Data/04 Data Formats" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Handling-Data-Data-Formats" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <meta name="tag" content="data event handlers"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="tradebars event"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="ticks event"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="splits event"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="dividends event"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="delistings event"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="symbol changed event"> 
          <p> There are six financial data types: TradeBars, Ticks, Delistings, SymbolChangedEvents, Splits and Dividends. </p> 
          <p> All data extends from <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic7983.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open BaseData API Documentation">BaseData </a> - the core data class which provides Symbol, Time and Value properties. </p> 
          <p> <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic8092.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open TradeBar API Documentation">TradeBar </a> events contains Open, High, Low, Close and Volume properties for a given period of time. </p> 
          <p> <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic23324.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open Dividend API Documentation">Dividend </a> events are triggered on payment of a dividend. It provides the Distribution per share. </p> 
          <p> <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic8072.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open Split API Documentation">Split </a> events are triggered on a share split or reverse split event. It provides a SplitFactor and ReferencePrice. </p> 
          <p> <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic8073.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open SymbolChangedEvent API Documentation">SymbolChangedEvent </a> provide notice of new ticker names for stocks, or mergers of two tickers into one. It provides the OldSymbol and NewSymbol tickers. </p> 
          <p> <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic6943.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open Delisting API Documentation">Delisting </a> events provide notice an asset is no longer trading on the exchange. </p> 
          <p> <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic23673.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open Ticks API Documentation">Ticks </a> is a string indexed dictionary of lists of ticks. </p> 
          <p class="csharp"> These data types all have dedicated event handlers which follow the pattern above (<code>public void OnData(Type data) {}</code>); and are also passed into the OnData(Slice data) event handler. </p> 
          <p class="python"> All these data types are accessible through their properties on the slice object. i.e. </p>
          <ul> 
           <li><code>slice.Bars</code></li> 
           <li><code>slice.Ticks</code></li> 
           <li><code>slice.Splits</code></li> 
           <li><code>slice.Dividends</code></li> 
           <li><code>slice.Delistings</code></li> 
           <li><code>slice.SymbolChangedEvents</code></li> 
          </ul> 
          <p></p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">//TradeBars collection of TradeBar objects
TradeBars data; TradeBar ibm = data["IBM"];

//Dividends collection of Dividend objects
Dividends data; Dividend ibm = data["IBM"];</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section"> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12"> 
         <h2 id="Importing-Custom-Data"> Importing Custom Data <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/04 Importing Custom Data" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true" style="font-size:0.7em;"></i> </a> <a href="#Importing-Custom-Data" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h2> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container"></div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Importing-Custom-Data-Introduction-to-Custom-Data"> Introduction to Custom Data <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/04 Importing Custom Data/01 Introduction to Custom Data" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Importing-Custom-Data-Introduction-to-Custom-Data" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <meta name="tag" content="custom data"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="quandl data"> 
          <p> LEAN supports backtesting almost any external custom data source. To use this feature you need to add the data during initialize using <code class="csharp">AddData&lt;T&gt;()</code> <code class="python">self.AddData()</code> and instruct your algorithm how to read your data. We provide helpers for popular data sources like Quandl, but if you are using your own format or server you'll need to create a custom type. </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Importing-Custom-Data-Initializing-Custom-Data"> Initializing Custom Data <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/04 Importing Custom Data/02 Initializing Custom Data" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Importing-Custom-Data-Initializing-Custom-Data" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <meta name="tag" content="custom data"> 
          <p> During initialize your algorithm must use <span class="csharp"> <code>AddData&lt;T&gt;(string ticker, Resolution resolution = Resolution.Daily)</code>. This gives LEAN the T-type factory to create the objects, the name of the data and the resolution at which to poll the data to check for updates. </span> <span class="python"> <code>self.AddData(Type class, string ticker, Resolution resolution = Resolution.Daily)</code>. This gives LEAN the type factory to create the data objects and the resolution to poll the remote datasource for updates. </span> </p> 
          <p> The framework checks for new data every as instructed by the <code>Resolution</code> period, i.e. Resolution.Tick polls constantly, Resolution.Second polls every second, and Resolution.Minute every minute. Hourly and Daily Resolutions are polled every 30 minutes to prevent skipping a day if the data was emitted late. </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">// In Initialize method:
AddData&lt;Weather&gt;("KNYC", Resolution.Daily);</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python"># In Initialize method:
self.AddData(Weather, "KNYC", Resolution.Minute)</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style="border-bottom: 1px solid #eee; "> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Importing-Custom-Data-Creating-and-Reading-Custom-Data"> Creating and Reading Custom Data <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/04 Importing Custom Data/03 Creating and Reading Custom Data" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Importing-Custom-Data-Creating-and-Reading-Custom-Data" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <meta name="tag" content="custom data"> 
          <p> You must create a custom type to instruct LEAN where to get your data, and how to read it. We support many different data types and formats. You can even change source locations for backtesting and live modes. All data must extend from <code>BaseData</code> and override the <code>Reader</code> and <code>GetSource</code> methods. </p> 
          <p> <code>GetSource</code> instructs LEAN where to find your data. It must return a <code>SubscriptionDataSource</code> object containing the string Url to find your data, and the format of the data (SubscriptionTransportMedium RemoteFile or Rest). When the source returned changes URL the data is downloaded again. This allows LEAN to cache large files and only download new data when requested. This also allows you to break up large intraday data into smaller daily files, speeding up the backtest. </p> 
          <p> When using <code>SubscriptionTransportMedium.Rest</code> the url provided is polled at each Resolution time step and is assumed to be sufficient for 1-data point. This is generally intended for live data sources. </p> 
          <p> <code>Reader</code> takes one line of data provided by the source, and parses it into one of your custom objects (e.g. Yahoo in the code snippet). In addition to setting your custom type properties, you should also take care to set three required properties: </p>
          <ol> 
           <li> Symbol - Should always be set to config.Symbol </li> 
           <li> Time - Required synchronization of custom data </li> 
           <li> Value - Required for purchasing and portfolio calculations </li> 
          </ol> 
          <p></p> 
          <p> When there is no usable data in a line, your type should return null. </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">public class Weather : BaseData
{
    public decimal MaxC = 0;
    public decimal MinC = 0;
    public string errString = "";

    public override SubscriptionDataSource GetSource(
        SubscriptionDataConfig config, 
        DateTime date, 
        bool isLive)
    {
        var source = string.Format(
                "https://www.wunderground.com/history/airport/{0}/{1}/1/1/CustomHistory.html?dayend=31&amp;monthend=12&amp;yearend={1}&amp;format=1",
                config.Symbol, date.Year);

          return new SubscriptionDataSource(source,
              SubscriptionTransportMedium.RemoteFile);
    }

    public override BaseData Reader(
        SubscriptionDataConfig config,
        string line,
        DateTime date,
        bool isLive)
    {
        if (string.IsNullOrWhiteSpace(line) ||
            char.IsLetter(line[0])) 
            return null;
            
        var data = line.Split(',');

        return new Weather()
        {
            // Make sure we only get this data AFTER trading day - don't want forward bias.
            Time = DateTime.Parse(data[0]).AddHours(20), 
            Symbol = config.Symbol,
            MaxC = Convert.ToDecimal(data[1]),
            Value = Convert.ToDecimal(data[2]),
            MinC = Convert.ToDecimal(data[3]),
        };
    }
}</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python">class Weather(PythonData):
    ''' Weather based rebalancing'''
    
    def GetSource(self, config, date, isLive):
        source = "https://www.wunderground.com/history/airport/{0}/{1}/1/1/CustomHistory.html?dayend=31&amp;monthend=12&amp;yearend={1}&amp;format=1".format(config.Symbol, date.year);
        return SubscriptionDataSource(source, SubscriptionTransportMedium.RemoteFile);       


    def Reader(self, config, line, date, isLive):
        # If first character is not digit, pass
        if not (line.strip() and line[0].isdigit()): return None
        
        data = line.split(',')
        weather = Weather()
        weather.Symbol = config.Symbol
        weather.Time = datetime.strptime(data[0], '%Y-%m-%d') + timedelta(hours=20) # Make sure we only get this data AFTER trading day - don't want forward bias.
        weather.Value = decimal.Decimal(data[2])
        weather["MaxC"] = float(data[1])
        weather["MinC"] = float(data[3])

        return weather</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section"> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12"> 
         <h2 id="Consolidating-Data"> Consolidating Data <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/05 Consolidating Data" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true" style="font-size:0.7em;"></i> </a> <a href="#Consolidating-Data" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h2> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container"></div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Consolidating-Data-Consolidating-data"> <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/05 Consolidating Data/01 Consolidating data" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Consolidating-Data-Consolidating-data" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <meta name="tag" content="consolidating data"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="using data"> 
          <p> Consolidators are used to combine smaller data points into larger bars. Commonly this is used to create 5, 10 or 15 minute bars from minute data. We provide tick, second, minute, hour and daily resolution bars which can be consolidated into any form you wish. </p> 
          <p> To use consolidators you create the consolidator class and then register it to receive data. Once you've registered the class it automatically gets data updates. Once it has aggregated the desired data it emits an event on the <code>DataConsolidated</code> event handler. You setup the consolidator and bind to this event handler once from inside your <code>Initialize()</code> method to prevent your algorithm from running out of memory. </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">// Create and initialize a consolidator
public override void Initialize()
{
	//...other initialization...
	AddEquity("SPY", Resolution.Minute);
	var consolidator = new TradeBarConsolidator(15);
	consolidator.DataConsolidated += {
		Debug(Time.ToString() + " &gt; New Bar!");
	};
	SubscriptionManager.AddConsolidator("SPY", consolidator);
}</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python"># Create and initialize a consolidator
def Initialize(self):
    # ...other initialization...
    self.AddEquity("SPY", Resolution.Minute)
    consolidator = TradeBarConsolidator(15)
    consolidator.DataConsolidated += self.OnDataConsolidated
    self.SubscriptionManager.AddConsolidator("SPY", consolidator)

def OnDataConsolidated(self, sender, bar):
    self.Debug(str(self.Time) + " &gt; New Bar!")</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Consolidating-Data-TradeBars-vs-QuoteBars"> TradeBars vs QuoteBars <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/05 Consolidating Data/02 TradeBars vs QuoteBars" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Consolidating-Data-TradeBars-vs-QuoteBars" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <meta name="tag" content="using data"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="assets"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="options"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="futures"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="forex"> 
          <p> The specific consolidator you should use depends on the data and assets you're requesting. TradeBars should be consolidated with a <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic8468.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open TradeBarConsolidator API Documentation">TradeBarConsolidator </a> ; QuoteBars with a <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic8385.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open QuoteBarConsolidator API Documentation">QuoteBarConsolidator </a> and Ticks with a <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic8445.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open TickConsolidator API Documentation">TickConsolidator </a> . Quote tick data must be consolidated by the <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic8456.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open TickQuoteBarConsolidator API Documentation">TickQuoteBarConsolidator </a> . </p> 
          <p> For each asset class and the data we provide please see the <a href="/data">data library</a>. It is a little confusing but here is the summary of QuantConnect provided data: </p> 
          <p> </p>
          <ul> 
           <li> Equities - trade data only. For Resolution.Tick use the TickConsolidator, for all other resolutions use the TradeBarConsolidator. </li> 
           <li> Forex and CFD - quote data only. For Resolution.Tick use the TickQuoteBarConsolidator, for all other resolutions use the QuoteBarConsolidators. </li> 
           <li> Options- trade and quote data, at Resolution.Minute only. For consolidating options data use the TradeBarConsolidator or the QuoteBarConsolidator (depending on if you're consolidating trades or quotes). </li> 
           <li> Futures - trade and quote data, at all resolutions! </li> 
          </ul> 
          <p></p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style="border-bottom: 1px solid #eee; "> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Consolidating-Data-Consolidators--Indicators"> Consolidators Indicators <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/05 Consolidating Data/03 Consolidators  Indicators" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Consolidating-Data-Consolidators--Indicators" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <meta name="tag" content="indicators"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="data event handlers"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="indicator helpers"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="consolidating data"> 
          <p> If you'd like to have an indicator updated using a specific resolution of data; e.g. 30-period, 15-minute EMA; then you should ideally use the helper methods which come with the indicators. Most indicators handle setting up these resolution periods for you. See <a href="#Indicators">Indicators</a> for more information. </p> 
          <p> You may have a custom indicator which doesn't have this helper. In this case you should register your indicator with the <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic312.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open RegisterIndicator API Documentation">RegisterIndicator </a> function which will automatically create a consolidator and pipe the data into your Indicator class. </p> 
          <p> In very rare cases you may want to update your indicator manually. You can do this by passing each data point into your <code>indicator.Update()</code> method from your consolidator <code>DataConsolidated</code> event handler. </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">// Consolidating minute SPY into Daily SMA/EMA.
var ema = EMA("SPY", 14, Resolution.Daily);
var sma = SMA("SPY", 14, Resolution.Daily);</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">// Register for daily bars from minutely data.
AddEquity("SPY", Resolution.Minute);
var myTradeBarIndicator = new MyTradeBarIndicator(120);
RegisterIndicator("SPY", myTradeBarIndicator, Resolution.Daily);</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python"># Consolidating minute SPY into Daily SMA/EMA.
ema = self.EMA("SPY", 14, Resolution.Daily)
sma = self.SMA("SPY", 14, Resolution.Daily)</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python"># Register for daily bars from minutely data.
self.AddEquity("SPY", Resolution.Minute)
myTradeBarIndicator = MyTradeBarIndicator(120)
self.RegisterIndicator("SPY", myTradeBarIndicator, Resolution.Daily)</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">// Create, initialize a consolidator and add an indicator
private SimpleMovingAverage _sma;

public override void Initialize()
{
	//...other initialization...
	AddEquity("SPY", Resolution.Minute);
	var consolidator = new TradeBarConsolidator(30);
	_sma = new SimpleMovingAverage(10);
	RegisterIndicator("SPY", _sma, consolidator);
	SubscriptionManager.AddConsolidator("SPY", consolidator);
}</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python"># Create, initialize a consolidator and add an indicator
def Initialize(self):
    # ...other initialization...
    self.AddEquity("SPY", Resolution.Minute)
    consolidator = TradeBarConsolidator(30)
    self._sma = SimpleMovingAverage(10)
    self.RegisterIndicator("SPY", self._sma, consolidator)
    self.SubscriptionManager.AddConsolidator("SPY", consolidator)</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section"> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12"> 
         <h2 id="Securities-and-Portfolio"> Securities and Portfolio <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/06 Securities and Portfolio" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true" style="font-size:0.7em;"></i> </a> <a href="#Securities-and-Portfolio" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h2> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container"></div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style="border-bottom: 1px solid #eee; "> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Securities-and-Portfolio-Securities-and-Portfolio-Classes"> Securities and Portfolio Classes <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/06 Securities and Portfolio/01 Securities and Portfolio Classes" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Securities-and-Portfolio-Securities-and-Portfolio-Classes" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <meta name="tag" content="securities and portfolio"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="securities"> 
          <p> Algorithms have a <code>Securities</code> property which stores a <code>Security</code> object for each asset in your algorithm. Security objects hold the models (backtesting behaviors) and properties of an asset. Each security can be completely customized to behave as you'd like. Securities is a <code>Dictionary&lt;Symbol, Security&gt;</code> so you can access your Security objects with their ticker <code>Securities["IBM"].Price</code>. </p> 
          <p> </p>
          <pre class="csharp">
// Popular Securities Property Values:
Securities["IBM"].HasData           // Security has data 
                 .Invested          // Have holdings
                 .LocalTime         // Time on the asset exchange
                 .Holdings          // Portfolio object
                 .Exchange          // Exchange information
                 .FeeModel;         // Fee model setter
</pre> 
          <p></p> 
          <p> Security objects also carry all the models for creating realistic backtests. These models are set via the public security properties and then used in LEAN to improve your backtest realism. </p> 
          <p> The Portfolio property is a collection of SecurityHolding objects to provide easy access to the holding properties. The Portfolio class is a <code>Dictionary&lt;Symbol, SecurityHolding&gt;</code> so can be accessed via ticker index: <code>Portfolio["IBM"].IsLong</code> </p> 
          <p> </p>
          <pre class="csharp">
// Popular Portfolio Property Values:
Portfolio["IBM"].Invested 
                .IsLong            // IsLong, IsShort Holdings.
                .Quantity          // Shares held.
                .UnrealizedProfit; // Holdings profit/loss
                .TotalFees         // Fees incurred since backtest start
                .Price;            // Asset price
</pre> 
          <p></p> 
          <p> Detailed information on these classes can be found in LEAN documentation. Check out the <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic445.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open Security API Documentation">Security </a> class (Securities objects), and <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic26002.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open SecurityHolding API Documentation">SecurityHolding </a> (Portfolio objects) classes. </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">//Securities array access to Security Objects:
Securities["IBM"].Price</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">//Security object properties:
class Security {
    Resolution Resolution;
    bool HasData;
    bool Invested;
    DateTime LocalTime;
    SecurityHolding Holdings;
    SecurityExchange Exchange;
    IFeeModel FeeModel;
    IFillModel FillModel;
    ISlippageModel SlippageModel;
    ISecurityPortfolioModel PortfolioModel;
    ISecurityMarginModel MarginModel;
    ISettlementModel SettlementModel;
    IVolatilityModel VolatilityModel;
    ISecurityDataFilter DataFilter;
}</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python">#Securities array access to Security Objects:
self.Securities["IBM"].Price</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">//Security object properties:
class Security {
    Resolution Resolution;
    bool HasData;
    bool Invested;
    DateTime LocalTime;
    SecurityHolding Holdings;
    SecurityExchange Exchange;
    IFeeModel FeeModel;
    IFillModel FillModel;
    ISlippageModel SlippageModel;
    ISecurityPortfolioModel PortfolioModel;
    ISecurityMarginModel MarginModel;
    ISettlementModel SettlementModel;
    IVolatilityModel VolatilityModel;
    ISecurityDataFilter DataFilter;
}</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section"> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12"> 
         <h2 id="Trading-and-Orders"> Trading and Orders <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/07 Trading and Orders" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true" style="font-size:0.7em;"></i> </a> <a href="#Trading-and-Orders" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h2> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container"></div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Trading-and-Orders-Key-Concepts"> Key Concepts <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/07 Trading and Orders/01 Key Concepts" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Trading-and-Orders-Key-Concepts" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <meta name="tag" content="trading and orders"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="placing orders"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="updating orders"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="managing orders"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="transactions"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="locating orders"> 
          <p> Algorithms can place an order through calling the appropriate method in the API. Going long is denoted with a ordering positive number, and short a negative one. LEAN does not support hedging (long and short at the same time). </p> 
          <p> Placing an order generates an <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic24531.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open OrderTicket API Documentation">OrderTicket </a> which you can use to update, cancel or check the status of your order. </p> 
          <p> To update an order can call the Update method on the OrderTicket. The Update method takes an <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic24611.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open UpdateOrderFields API Documentation">UpdateOrderFields </a> object which defines what properties of the order should be updated. In the same way you can cancel your order with the OrderTicket Cancel method. </p> 
          <p> The OrderTicket Status property can be used to determine if the order is filled. The <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic24346.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open OrderStatus API Documentation">OrderStatus </a> has the values Submitted, PartiallyFilled, Filled, Cancelled or Invalid. </p> 
          <p> The Transactions property is a helper that provides easy access to current and past orders and order tickets. </p> 
          <p> </p>
          <pre>
// Popular Transactions methods:
Transactions
            .CancelOpenOrders(Symbol symbol)
            .CancelOrder(int orderId, string orderTag = null)
            .GetOpenOrders()
            .GetOpenOrders(Symbol symbol)
            .GetOrderById(int orderId)
            .GetOrders(Func
           <order, bool>
            
	 filter)            .GetOrderTicket(int orderId)            .GetOrderTickets(Func
	
            <orderticket, bool>
              filter = null)
            </orderticket,>
           </order,></pre> 
          <p></p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">// Creating an Order:
OrderTicket limitOrderTicket = LimitOrder("SPY", 100, 205);

// Updating an Order:
limitOrderTicket.Update(new UpdateOrderFields{LimitPrice = 207.50};

// Cancel an Order:
limitOrderTicket.Cancel();</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python"># Creating an Order:
limitOrderTicket = self.LimitOrder("SPY", 100, 205)

# Updating an Order:
updateOrderFields = UpdateOrderFields()
updateOrderFields.LimitPrice = decimal.Decimal(207.50)
limitOrderTicket.Update(updateOrderFields)

# Cancel an Order:
limitOrderTicket.Cancel()</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">// Cancel all open orders from SPY
List&lt;OrderTicket&gt; cancelledOrders = Transactions.CancelOpenOrders("SPY")

// Cancel order #10
OrderTicket cancelledOrder = Transactions.CancelOrder(10);

// Get open orders
List&lt;Order&gt; openOrders = Transactions.GetOpenOrders();
List&lt;Order&gt; openOrders = Transactions
    .GetOrders(x =&gt; x.Status.IsOpen()).ToList();

// Get open orders from SPY
List&lt;Order&gt; openOrders = Transactions.GetOpenOrders("SPY");
List&lt;Order&gt; openOrders = Transactions
    .GetOrders(x =&gt; x.Status.IsOpen() &amp;&amp; x.Symbol == "SPY").ToList();

// Get open order #10
Order openOrder = Transactions.GetOrderById(10);

// Get order ticket #10
OrderTicket orderTicket = Transactions.GetOrderTicket(10);

// Get open orders tickets from SPY
IEnumerable&lt;OrderTicket&gt; openOrderTickets = Transactions
    .GetOrderTickets(x =&gt; x.Status.IsOpen() &amp;&amp; x.Symbol == "SPY");</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python"># Cancel all open orders from SPY
cancelledOrders = self.Transactions.CancelOpenOrders("SPY")

# Cancel order #10
cancelledOrder = self.Transactions.CancelOrder(10)

# Get open orders
openOrders = self.Transactions.GetOpenOrders()

# Get open orders from SPY
openOrders = self.Transactions.GetOpenOrders("SPY")

# Get open order #10
openOrder = self.Transactions.GetOrderById(10)

# Get all orders
orders = self.Transactions.GetOrders()

# Get order ticket #10
orderTicket = self.Transactions.GetOrderTicket(10)

# Get all orders tickets
openOrderTickets = self.Transactions.GetOrderTickets()</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Trading-and-Orders-Set-Holdings-Helper"> Set Holdings Helper <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/07 Trading and Orders/02 Set Holdings Helper" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Trading-and-Orders-Set-Holdings-Helper" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <meta name="tag" content="trading and orders"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="placing orders"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="portfolio helpers"> 
          <p> Often portfolio based algorithms want to set the portfolio based on percentage weighting. We provide a helper method to perform this weighting for you called <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic364.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open SetHoldings API Documentation">SetHoldings </a> . </p>
          <pre class="prettyprint">
SetHoldings(Symbol symbol, double percentage, bool liquidateExistingHoldings = false)
</pre> 
          <p></p> 
          <p> When liquidate existing holdings is set to true any existing holdings will first be sold. This may be useful when you're rebalancing to a new set of stocks. The <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic229.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open Liquidate API Documentation">Liquidate </a> method can achieve the same affect.</p>
          <pre class="prettyprint">
Liquidate(Symbol symbolToLiquidate = null)
</pre>Liquidate sells all holdings in your portfolio, or just the ticker symbol if the parameter is specified. 
          <p></p> 
          <p> SetHoldings sets a fraction of unlevered equity. e.g. If you have 2x available leverage, and SetHoldings to 1.0 the algorithm will use 1.0 of your available buying power. To maximize buying power in this case you would make the SetHoldings fractions total 2.0. </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">// Set fixed percentages of known tickers:
SetHoldings("IBM", 0.25);
SetHoldings("GOOG", 0.25);
SetHoldings("AAPL", 0.25);
SetHoldings("MSFT", 0.25);

// Or set portfolio to equal weighting of all securities:
var weighting = 1m / Securities.Count;
foreach(var security in Securities.Values) {
    SetHoldings(security.Symbol, weighting);
}</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python"># Set fixed percentages of known tickers:
self.SetHoldings("IBM", 0.25)
self.SetHoldings("GOOG", 0.25)
self.SetHoldings("AAPL", 0.25)
self.SetHoldings("MSFT", 0.25)

# Or set portfolio to equal weighting of all securities:
weighting = 1.0 / self.Securities.Count
for security in self.Securities.Values:
    self.SetHoldings(security.Symbol, weighting)</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Trading-and-Orders-Order-Types"> Order Types <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/07 Trading and Orders/03 Order Types" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Trading-and-Orders-Order-Types" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <meta name="tag" content="trading and orders"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="placing orders"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="order types"> 
          <p> We support many different order types. In live trading some of these order types may be simulated depending on your brokerage (for more information on this see <a href="#Live-Trading">Live Trading</a>). </p>
          <table class="table table-striped csharp"> 
           <thead> 
            <tr> 
             <th> Order Type </th> 
             <th> Method Signature </th> 
            </tr> 
           </thead> 
           <tbody> 
            <tr> 
             <td> Market Order </td> 
             <td> <pre class="prettyprint">MarketOrder(Symbol symbol, int quantity, bool asynchronous = false, string tag = "")</pre> <small>Asynchronous flag can be used to send the many orders and not wait for the fill response.</small> </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> Market On Open </td> 
             <td> <pre class="prettyprint">MarketOnOpenOrder(Symbol symbol, int quantity, string tag = "")</pre> <small>Fill an order at the market opening. Equity markets only.</small> </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> Market On Close </td> 
             <td> <pre class="prettyprint">MarketOnCloseOrder(Symbol symbol, int quantity, string tag = "")</pre> <small>Fill an order on market closing. Equity markets only. Orders must be submitted 15min before closing.</small> </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> Stop Market </td> 
             <td> <pre class="prettyprint">StopMarketOrder(Symbol symbol, int quantity, decimal stopPrice, string tag = "")</pre> <small>Submit a market order when the stop price is reached.</small> </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> Limit Order </td> 
             <td> <pre class="prettyprint">LimitOrder(Symbol symbol, int quantity, decimal limitPrice, string tag = "")</pre> <small>Fill order for the limit price or better.</small> </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> Stop Limit Order </td>
