             <td> <pre class="prettyprint">StopLimitOrder(Symbol symbol, int quantity, decimal stopPrice, decimal limitPrice, string tag = "")</pre> <small>Submit limit order when stop price is reached.</small> </td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody>
          </table> All order methods return an OrderTicket. The tag parameter can be used to send additional debugging information along with each order object. 
          <p></p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">// Various order types:
// Fill a market order immediately (before moving to next line of code)
var newTicket = MarketOrder("IBM", 100);

// Place a long limit order with limit price less than current price
var newTicket = LimitOrder("IBM", 100, lastClose * .999m);

// Closing out a short position; long stop above the last close price
var stopPrice = close * 1.0025m;
var newTicket = StopMarketOrder("IBM", 100, stopPrice);

// Closing out a long position on market drop
var stopPrice = close * .9975m;
var newTicket = StopMarketOrder("IBM", -100, stopPrice);

// Limit order trigger on reaching the stop price
var newTicket = StopLimitOrder("IBM", 100, stopPrice, limitPrice);

// Market on Open/Close:
var newTicket = MarketOnCloseOrder("IBM", 100);
var newTicket = MarketOnOpenOrder("IBM", 100);</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python"># Various order types:
# Fill a market order immediately (before moving to next line of code)
newTicket = self.MarketOrder("IBM", 100)

# Place a long limit order with limit price less than current price
newTicket = self.LimitOrder("IBM", 100, lastClose * decimal.Decimal(.999))

# Closing out a short position; long stop above the last close price
stopPrice = close * decimal.Decimal(1.0025)
newTicket = self.StopMarketOrder("IBM", 100, stopPrice)

# Closing out a long position on market drop
stopPrice = close * decimal.Decimal(.9975)
newTicket = self.StopMarketOrder("IBM", -100, stopPrice)

# Limit order trigger on reaching the stop price
newTicket = self.StopLimitOrder("IBM", 100, stopPrice, limitPrice)

# Market on Open/Close:
newTicket = self.MarketOnCloseOrder("IBM", 100)
newTicket = self.MarketOnOpenOrder("IBM", 100)</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Trading-and-Orders-Order-Events"> Order Events <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/07 Trading and Orders/04 Order Events" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Trading-and-Orders-Order-Events" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <meta name="tag" content="data event handlers"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="order events"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="trading and orders"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="order events"> 
          <p> Orders create lots of events you can use to track their status. These events are passed into the <code>OnOrderEvent</code> event handler with the relevant order. </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">// Override the base class event handler for order events
public override void OnOrderEvent(OrderEvent orderEvent)
{
    var order = Transactions.GetOrderById(orderEvent.OrderId);
    Console.WriteLine("{0}: {1}: {2}", Time, order.Type, orderEvent);
}</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python"># Override the base class event handler for order events
def OnOrderEvent(self, orderEvent):
    order = self.Transactions.GetOrderById(orderEvent.OrderId)
    self.Debug("{0}: {1}: {2}".format(self.Time, order.Type, orderEvent))</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style="border-bottom: 1px solid #eee; "> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Trading-and-Orders-Order-Error-Codes"> Order Error Codes <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/07 Trading and Orders/05 Order Error Codes" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Trading-and-Orders-Order-Error-Codes" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <meta name="tag" content="trading and orders"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="order errors"> 
          <p> When an order fails to process it is returned with a negative order code. These error codes mean different things as described below: </p> 
          <p> </p>
          <table class="table table-striped"> 
           <thead> 
            <tr> 
             <th style="width: 10%;"> Error Code </th> 
             <th> Interpretation </th> 
            </tr> 
           </thead> 
           <tbody> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>-1</b> </td> 
             <td style="text-align: left;"> <b>ProcessingError</b> - Unknown error. </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>-2</b> </td> 
             <td style="text-align: left;"> <b>OrderAlreadyExists</b> - Cannot submit because order already exists. </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>-3</b> </td> 
             <td style="text-align: left;"> <b>InsufficientBuyingPower</b> - Not enough money to to submit order. </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>-4</b> </td> 
             <td style="text-align: left;"> <b>BrokerageModelRefusedToSubmitOrder</b> - Internal logic invalidated submit order. </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>-5</b> </td> 
             <td style="text-align: left;"> <b>BrokerageFailedToSubmitOrder</b> - Brokerage rejected order. </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>-6</b> </td> 
             <td style="text-align: left;"> <b>BrokerageFailedToUpdateOrder</b> - Failed to update order. </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>-7</b> </td> 
             <td style="text-align: left;"> <b>BrokerageHandlerRefusedToUpdateOrder</b> - Brokerage rejected update request. </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>-8</b> </td> 
             <td style="text-align: left;"> <b>BrokerageFailedToCancelOrder</b> - Brokerage refused to cancel order. </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>-9</b> </td> 
             <td style="text-align: left;"> <b>InvalidOrderStatus</b> - Only pending orders can be cancelled </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>-10</b> </td> 
             <td style="text-align: left;"> <b>UnableToFindOrder</b> - Cannot find order with that id. </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>-11</b> </td> 
             <td style="text-align: left;"> <b>OrderQuantityZero</b> - Cannot submit or update orders with zero quantity. </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>-12</b> </td> 
             <td style="text-align: left;"> <b>UnsupportedRequestType</b> - This type of request is unsupported. </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>-13</b> </td> 
             <td style="text-align: left;"> <b>PreOrderChecksError</b> - Pre-placement order checks failed. </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>-14</b> </td> 
             <td style="text-align: left;"> <b>MissingSecurity</b> - Security is missing. Probably did not subscribe. </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>-15</b> </td> 
             <td style="text-align: left;"> <b>ExchangeNotOpen</b> - Some order types require open exchange. </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>-16</b> </td> 
             <td style="text-align: left;"> <b>SecurityPriceZero</b> - There isn't any market data yet for the security. </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>-17</b> </td> 
             <td style="text-align: left;"> <b>ForexBaseAndQuoteCurrenciesRequired</b> - Need both currencies in cashbook to trade a pair. </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>-18</b> </td> 
             <td style="text-align: left;"> <b>ForexConversionRateZero</b> - Need conversion rate to account currency. </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>-19</b> </td> 
             <td style="text-align: left;"> <b>SecurityHasNoData</b> - Should not attempt trading without at least one data point. </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>-20</b> </td> 
             <td style="text-align: left;"> <b>ExceededMaximumOrders</b> - Transaction manager's cache is full. </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>-21</b> </td> 
             <td style="text-align: left;"> <b>MarketOnCloseOrderTooLate</b> - Need to submit market on close orders at least 11 minutes before exchange close. </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>-22</b> </td> 
             <td style="text-align: left;"> <b>InvalidRequest</b> - Request is invalid or null. </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>-23</b> </td> 
             <td style="text-align: left;"> <b>RequestCanceled</b> - Request was canceled by user. </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>-24</b> </td> 
             <td style="text-align: left;"> <b>AlgorithmWarmingUp</b> - All orders are invalidated while algorithm is warming up. </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>-25</b> </td> 
             <td style="text-align: left;"> <b>BrokerageModelRefusedToUpdateOrder</b> - Internal logic invalidated update order. </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>-26</b> </td> 
             <td style="text-align: left;"> <b>QuoteCurrencyRequired</b> - Need quote currency in cashbook to trade. </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>-27</b> </td> 
             <td style="text-align: left;"> <b>ConversionRateZero</b> - Need conversion rate to account currency. </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>-28</b> </td> 
             <td style="text-align: left;"> <b>NonTradableSecurity</b> - The order's symbol references a non-tradable security. </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>-29</b> </td> 
             <td style="text-align: left;"> <b>NonExercisableSecurity</b> - The order's symbol references a non-exercisable security. </td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody> 
          </table>

         <h2 id="Scheduled-Events"> Scheduled Events <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/08 Scheduled Events" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true" style="font-size:0.7em;"></i> </a> <a href="#Scheduled-Events" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h2> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container"></div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Scheduled-Events-Introduction-to-Scheduled-Events"> Introduction to Scheduled Events <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/08 Scheduled Events/01 Introduction to Scheduled Events" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Scheduled-Events-Introduction-to-Scheduled-Events" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <meta name="tag" content="scheduled events"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="date rules"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="time rules"> 
          <p> Scheduled events allow you to trigger code to run at specific times of day. This happens regardless of your data events. The schedule API requires a date and time rule to specify when the event is fired. </p> 
          <p> Scheduled events need a <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic25183.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open DateRules API Documentation">DateRules </a> and <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic451.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open TimeRules API Documentation">TimeRules </a> pair to set a specific time. When the event is triggered the action block is executed. </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style="border-bottom: 1px solid #eee; "> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Scheduled-Events-DateTime-Rules"> DateTime Rules <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/08 Scheduled Events/02 DateTime Rules" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Scheduled-Events-DateTime-Rules" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <meta name="tag" content="scheduled events"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="date rules"> 
          <meta name="tag" content="time rules"> 
          <p> </p>
          <table class="table table-striped"> 
           <thead> 
            <tr> 
             <th style="width: 30%;"> DateRules Class </th> 
             <th> Example Usage </th> 
            </tr> 
           </thead> 
           <tbody> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>On(year,month,day)</b> </td> 
             <td> <pre class="prettyprint">DateRules.On(2013, 10, 7)</pre> <small>Trigger an event on a specific date.</small> </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>EveryDay(symbol)</b> </td> 
             <td> <pre class="prettyprint">DateRules.EveryDay("SPY")</pre> <small>Trigger an event every day a specific symbol is trading.</small> </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>EveryDay()</b> </td> 
             <td> <pre class="prettyprint">DateRules.EveryDay()</pre> <small>Trigger an event every day.</small> </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>Every(days)</b> </td> 
             <td> <pre class="prettyprint">DateRules.Every(DayOfWeek.Monday, DayOfWeek.Friday)</pre> <small>Trigger an event on specific days during week.</small> </td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody> 
          </table> 
          <p></p> 
          <p> </p>
          <table class="table table-striped"> 
           <thead> 
            <tr> 
             <th style="width: 30%;"> TimeRules Class </th> 
             <th> Example Usage </th> 
            </tr> 
           </thead> 
           <tbody> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>At(hour, min)</b> </td> 
             <td> <pre class="prettyprint">TimeRules.At(13, 10)</pre> <small>Trigger an event at a specific time of day (e.g. 13:10).</small> </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>AfterMarketOpen(symbol, min)</b> </td> 
             <td> <pre class="prettyprint">TimeRules.AfterMarketOpen("SPY", 10)</pre> <small>Trigger an event a few minutes after market open for a specific symbol.</small> </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>BeforeMarketClose(symbol, min)</b> </td> 
             <td> <pre class="prettyprint">TimeRules.BeforeMarketClose("SPY", 10)</pre> <small>Trigger an event a few minutes before close for a specific symbol.</small> </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>Every(period)</b> </td> 
             <td> <pre class="prettyprint">TimeRules.Every(TimeSpan.FromMinutes(10))</pre> <small>Trigger an event every period interval.</small> </td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody> 
          </table> 
          <p></p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">// Schedule an event to fire at a specific date/time
Schedule.On(DateRules.On(2013, 10, 7), TimeRules.At(13, 0), () =&gt;
{
	Log("SpecificTime: Fired at : " + Time);
});

// Schedule an event to fire every trading day for a security
// The time rule here tells it to fire 10 minutes after SPY's market open
Schedule.On(DateRules.EveryDay("SPY"), TimeRules.AfterMarketOpen("SPY", 10), () =&gt;
{
	Log("EveryDay.SPY 10 min after open: Fired at: " + Time);
});

// Schedule an event to fire every trading day for a security
// The time rule here tells it to fire 10 minutes before SPY's market close
Schedule.On(DateRules.EveryDay("SPY"), TimeRules.BeforeMarketClose("SPY", 10), () =&gt;
{
	Log("EveryDay.SPY 10 min before close: Fired at: " + Time);
});

// Schedule an event to fire on certain days of the week
Schedule.On(DateRules.Every(DayOfWeek.Monday, DayOfWeek.Friday), TimeRules.At(12, 0), () =&gt;
{
	Log("Mon/Fri at 12pm: Fired at: " + Time);
});</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python"># Schedule.On third argument type is System.Action or System.Action[System.String,System.DateTime]
# we need to cast the callback function using Action(...) to make it work

# schedule an event to fire at a specific date/time
self.Schedule.On(self.DateRules.On(2013, 10, 7), \ 
                 self.TimeRules.At(13, 0), \ 
                 Action(self.SpecificTime))

# schedule an event to fire every trading day for a security the
# time rule here tells it to fire 10 minutes after SPY's market open
self.Schedule.On(self.DateRules.EveryDay("SPY"), \ 
                 self.TimeRules.AfterMarketOpen(self.spy, 10), \        
                 Action(self.EveryDayAfterMarketOpen))

# schedule an event to fire every trading day for a security the
# time rule here tells it to fire 10 minutes before SPY's market close
self.Schedule.On(self.DateRules.EveryDay("SPY"), \
                 self.TimeRules.BeforeMarketClose("SPY", 10), \
                 Action(self.EveryDayAfterMarketClose))

# schedule an event to fire on certain days of the week
self.Schedule.On(self.DateRules.Every(DayOfWeek.Monday, DayOfWeek.Friday), \
                 self.TimeRules.At(12, 0), \
                 Action(self.EveryMonFriAtNoon))

# the scheduling methods return the ScheduledEvent object which can be used 
# for other things here I set the event up to check the portfolio value every
# 10 minutes, and liquidate if we have too many losses
self.Schedule.On(self.DateRules.EveryDay(), \ 
                 self.TimeRules.Every(timedelta(minutes=10)), \
                 Action(self.LiquidateUnrealizedLosses))

# schedule an event to fire at the beginning of the month, the symbol is
# optional. 
# if specified, it will fire the first trading day for that symbol of the month,
# if not specified it will fire on the first day of the month
self.Schedule.On(self.DateRules.MonthStart("SPY"), \
                 self.TimeRules.AfterMarketOpen("SPY"), \
                 Action(self.RebalancingCode))</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python">def SpecificTime(self):
    self.Log("SpecificTime: Fired at : {0}".format(self.Time))

def EveryDayAfterMarketOpen(self):
    self.Log("EveryDay.SPY 10 min after open: Fired at: {0}".format(self.Time))

def EveryDayAfterMarketClose(self):
    self.Log("EveryDay.SPY 10 min before close: Fired at: {0}".format(self.Time))

def EveryMonFriAtNoon(self):
    self.Log("Mon/Fri at 12pm: Fired at: {0}".format(self.Time))

def LiquidateUnrealizedLosses(self):
    ''' if we have over 1000 dollars in unrealized losses, liquidate'''
    if self.Portfolio.TotalUnrealizedProfit &lt; -1000:
        self.Log("Liquidated due to unrealized losses at: {0}".format(self.Time))
        self.Liquidate()

def RebalancingCode(self):
    ''' Good spot for rebalancing code?'''
    pass</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section"> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12"> 
         <h2 id="Indicators"> Indicators <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/09 Indicators" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true" style="font-size:0.7em;"></i> </a> <a href="#Indicators" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h2> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container"></div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Indicators-Indicator-Introduction"> Indicator Introduction <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/09 Indicators/01 Indicator Introduction" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Indicators-Indicator-Introduction" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <p> We provide more than 100 technical indicators for you to use in your algorithm. These are provided in two ways; through helper short cut methods, and as class objects. Indicators created through the short cut methods have already been wired up to receive data and are "ready to use". A full list of the indicators and their properties can be found in the reference table below. </p> 
          <p> One key indicator to learn is the <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic217.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open Identity API Documentation">Identity </a> indicator which simply returns the value of the asset. This can be useful for combining indicators together. For example:</p>
          <pre>var pep = Identity("PEP");    // Pepsi ticker
var coke = Identity("KO");    // Coke ticker
var delta = pep.Minus(coke);  // Difference between them
</pre> 
          <p></p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
        </div>

       </div>

        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">// 1. Using basic indicator at the same resolution as source security:
// TIP -&gt; You can use string "IBM" or the security.Symbol object
var ema = EMA("IBM", 14);

//2. Using indicator at different (higher) resolution to the source security:
var emaDaily = EMA("IBM", 14, Resolution.Daily);

//3. Indicator of a different property (default is close of bar/data):
// TIP -&gt; You can use helper methods Field.Open, Field.High etc on the indicator selector:
var emaDailyHigh = EMA("IBM", 14, Resolution.Daily, point =&gt; ((TradeBar) point).High);

//NOTE. Some indicators require tradebars (ATR, AROON) so your selector must return a TradeBar object for those indicators.</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python"># 1. Using basic indicator at the same resolution as source security:
ema = self.EMA("IBM", 14)

#2. Using indicator at different (higher) resolution to the source security:
emaDaily = self.EMA("IBM", 14, Resolution.Daily)

#3. Indicator of a different property (default is close of bar/data):
emaDailyHigh = self.EMA("IBM", 14, Resolution.Daily, Field.High)</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Indicators-Indicator-Extensions"> Indicator Extensions <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/09 Indicators/03 Indicator Extensions" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Indicators-Indicator-Extensions" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <p> Indicators are <i>composable</i> - meaning they can be <i>chained</i> together to create unique combinations much like lego blocks. We support several indicator extensions as outlined below: </p> 
          <p> </p>
          <table class="table table-striped csharp"> 
           <thead> 
            <tr> 
             <th> Extension </th> 
             <th> Example Usage </th> 
            </tr> 
           </thead> 
           <tbody> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>.Plus() </b></td> 
             <td> 
              <div class="indicators-method-usage">
                var emaSum = ema5.Plus(ema20); 
              </div> <small>Add a fixed value or indicator value to another indicator</small> </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>.Minus() </b></td> 
             <td> 
              <div class="indicators-method-usage">
                var emaDelta = ema20.Minus(ema5); 
              </div> <small>Find the difference between two indicators</small> </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>.Times() </b></td> 
             <td> 
              <div class="indicators-method-usage">
                var rsiSafe = rsi.Times(0.95); 
              </div> <small>Multiply one indicator or constant value by another.</small> </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>.Over() </b></td> 
             <td> 
              <div class="indicators-method-usage">
                var emaAverage = ema5.Plus(ema10).Over(2); 
              </div> <small>Divide indicator chain by constant or indicator.</small> </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>.Of() </b></td> 
             <td> 
              <div class="indicators-method-usage">
                var sma = new SimpleMovingAverage("SPY", 14); 
               <br> var rsiAverage= sma.Of( rsi ); 
              </div> <small>Feed an indicator output into input of another.</small> </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>.SMA(int period) </b></td> 
             <td> 
              <div class="indicators-method-usage">
                var rsiAvg = rsi.SMA(10); 
              </div> <small>Of extension helper for SMA method.</small> </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>.EMA(int period) </b></td> 
             <td> 
              <div class="indicators-method-usage">
                var rsiAvg = rsi.EMA(10); 
              </div> <small>Of extension helper for EMA method.</small> </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>.MAX(int period) </b></td> 
             <td> 
              <div class="indicators-method-usage">
                var rsiMax = rsi.MAX(10); 
              </div> <small>Of extension helper for MAX method, get max in i-samples.</small> </td> 
            </tr> 
            <tr> 
             <td> <b>.MIN(int period) </b></td> 
             <td> 
              <div class="indicators-method-usage">
                var rsiMin = rsi.MIN(10); 
              </div> <small>Of extension helper for MIN method, get min in i-samples.</small> </td> 
            </tr> 
           </tbody> 
          </table> 
          <p></p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">public class IndicatorTests : QCAlgorithm
{
    //Save off reference to indicator objects
    RelativeStrengthIndex _rsi;
    SimpleMovingAverage _rsiSMA;

    public override void Initialize()
    {
       //In addition to other initialize logic:
       _rsi = RSI("SPY", 14); // Creating a RSI
       _rsiSMA = _rsi.SMA(3); // Creating the SMA on the RSI
    }
    
    public override void OnData(Slice data)
    {
       Plot("RSI", _rsi, _rsiSMA);
    }
}</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div>

       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style="border-bottom: 1px solid #eee; "> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Indicators-Plotting-Indicators"> Plotting Indicators <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/09 Indicators/04 Plotting Indicators" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Indicators-Plotting-Indicators" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <p> A helper method makes plotting indicators simple. Further information about the charting API can be found in the <a href="#Charting">documentation below</a>.</p>
          <pre>Plot&lt;T&gt;(string chart, params IndicatorBase&lt;T&gt;[] indicators) where T : BaseData</pre>Note that not all indicators share the same base type(T) so may not work together. 
          <p></p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">//Plot array of indicator objects; extending "Indicator" type.
Plot("Indicators", sma, rsi); 

//Plot array of indicator objects; extending "TradeBarIndicator" type.
Plot("Indicators", atr, aroon); 

//For complex plotting it might be easiest to simply plot your indicators individually.</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python">#Plot array of indicator objects; extending "Indicator" type.
self.Plot("Indicators", sma, rsi); 

#Plot array of indicator objects; extending "TradeBarIndicator" type.
self.Plot("Indicators", atr, aroon); 

#Currently, there is a limit of 4 indicators for each Plot call
#For complex plotting it might be easiest to simply plot your indicators individually.</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section"> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12"> 
         <h2 id="Universes"> Universes <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/10 Universes" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true" style="font-size:0.7em;"></i> </a> <a href="#Universes" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h2> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container"></div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Universes-Introduction-to-Universes"> Introduction to Universes <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/10 Universes/01 Introduction to Universes" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Universes-Introduction-to-Universes" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <p> Often you may want to rotate securities in your algorithm based on filter criteria. You may only want equities above their 200 day EMA, or to only follow stocks on your custom list of symbols. This is possible using our <i>universe selection</i> API. </p> 
          <p> Universes are how LEAN organizes collections of data subscriptions under the hood. Each security and its data is controlled by a universe. When no universes are asking for data, the asset is removed from your algorithm. If your algorithm has open orders or holdings in a security we will not remove it from your subscriptions. </p> 
          <p> Every algorithm has a hidden "user-defined-universe". The assets in this universe are set by the <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic117.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open AddEquity API Documentation">AddEquity </a> / <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic118.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open AddForex API Documentation">AddForex </a> methods. These assets are fixed and never removed from your algorithm. </p> 
          <p> Universes are refreshed every day by default, but can be refreshed as often as required. This is controlled in the <code>algorithm.UniverseSettings</code> variable which we'll describe in more detail below. </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Universes-Basic-Universe-API"> Basic Universe API <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/10 Universes/02 Basic Universe API" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Universes-Basic-Universe-API" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <p> <b>Adding Universes</b> <br> Universes are added using the <code>AddUniverse()</code> method API. They are a type of data subscription which control what subscriptions are requested; and as such you can create <i>custom</i> universe data types. Depending on what type of universe you are adding there are many helper methods to make it easier. <code>AddUniverse()</code> methods take function filters as parameters, these filters must return an enumerable of Symbol objects. </p> 
          <p> <b>Universe Settings</b> <br> If you do not pass in a full universe object the <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic458.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open UniverseSettings API Documentation">UniverseSettings </a> property is used to fill in the blanks. Changing the UniverseSettings algorithm property can be helpful to simplify adding universes. Universes have 4 key properties:</p>
          <pre>
    //Popular universe settings:
    UniverseSettings.Resolution      // What resolution should added assets use
                    .Leverage        // What leverage should assets use in the universe?
                    .Fillforward     // Should asset data fill forward?
                    .MinimumTimeInUniverse // Minimum time assets should be in universe
                    .ExtendedMarketHours  // Should assets also feed extended market hours?
</pre> 
          <p></p> 
          <p> Once added universes are stored in the <code>IDictionary&lt;string, Universe&gt; UniverseManager</code>. </p> 
          <p> <b>Universe Events</b> <br> When universe contents are changed (securities are added or removed from the algorithm) we generate an <code>OnSecuritiesChanged</code> event. This allows your algorithm to know the changes in the universe state. The event passes in the <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic23864.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open SecurityChanges API Documentation">SecurityChanges </a> object containing references to the Added and Removed securities. </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">// Inside your initialize function:

// Subscriptions added via universe selection will have this resolution
UniverseSettings.Resolution = Resolution.Hour;

// Force securities to remain in the universe for a minimum of 30 days
UniverseSettings.MinimumTimeInUniverse = TimeSpan.FromDays(30);

// Helper: Add US-equity universe for the top 50 stocks by dollar volume
AddUniverse(Universe.DollarVolume.Top(50));

// Helper: Add US-equity universe for the bottom 50 stocks by dollar volume
AddUniverse(Universe.DollarVolume.Bottom(50));

// Helper: Add US-equity universe for the 90th dollar volume percentile
AddUniverse(Universe.DollarVolume.Percentile(90));

// Helper: Add US-equity universe for stocks between the 70th and 80th dollar volume percentile
AddUniverse(Universe.DollarVolume.Percentile(70, 80));</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">// Overriding the on changes event handler.
public override void OnSecuritiesChanged(SecurityChanges changes)
{
     _changes = changes;
}</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python"># Overriding the on changes event handler.
def OnSecuritiesChanged(self, changes):
     self._changes = changes</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">// Use UniverseManager to find symbols from the Universe Selection
foreach (var universe in UniverseManager.Values)
{    
    // User defined universe has symbols from AddSecurity/AddEquity calls
    if (universe is UserDefinedUniverse)
    {
        continue;
    }
    var symbols = universe.Members.Keys;
}</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python"># Use UniverseManager to find symbols from the Universe Selection
for universe in self.UniverseManager.Values:

    # User defined universe has symbols from AddSecurity/AddEquity calls
    if universe is UserDefinedUniverse:
        continue
    
    symbols = universe.Members.Keys</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Universes-Coarse-Universe-Selection"> Coarse Universe Selection <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/10 Universes/03 Coarse Universe Selection" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Universes-Coarse-Universe-Selection" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <p> Coarse Universe selection is the built in universe data provided by QuantConnect. Using financial data we generate a few key properties for each symbol and allow you to filter the universe of 16,400+ symbols to receive the symbols matching your filter criteria. It uses the <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic23747.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open CoarseFundamental API Documentation">CoarseFundamental </a> type. </p> 
          <p> Coarse fundamental has the following properties you can use to perform rough filtering.</p>
          <pre>class CoarseFundamental {
    public long Volume;             // Traded shares
    public decimal DollarVolume;    // Traded shares x Price
    public decimal Price;           // Yesterday close price
    public Symbol Symbol;           // Asset symbol
    public bool HasFundamentalData; // Whether it has fundamental
}</pre> 
          <p></p> 
          <p> Coarse filtering allows you to select an unlimited universe of symbols to analyse. You are only limited by practical memory and speed limits and may quickly run out of memory if you backtest too many symbols in parallel. These limits can be increased with a subscription. </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">// Take the top 50 by dollar volume using coarse 
AddUniverse(coarse =&gt; {
    return (from c in coarse
	    where c.Price &gt; 10
	    orderby c.DollarVolume descending 
            select c.Symbol).Take(50);
});</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python"># In Initialize:
self.AddUniverse(self.CoarseSelectionFunction)

def CoarseSelectionFunction(self, coarse):
    '''Take the top 50 by dollar volume using coarse'''
    # sort descending by daily dollar volume
    sortedByDollarVolume = sorted(coarse, \
        key=lambda x: x.DollarVolume, reverse=True) 

    # we need to return only the symbol objects
    return [ x.Symbol for x in sortedByDollarVolume[:50] ]</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">// We can use the following helper to reproduce the same result
AddUniverse(Universe.DollarVolume.Top(50));</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Universes-Fundamentals-Selection"> Fundamentals Selection <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/10 Universes/04 Fundamentals Selection" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Universes-Fundamentals-Selection" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <p> QuantConnect provides <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/data#provider/morningstar">Morningstar</a> corporate fundamentals data for US Equities symbols. The available dataset includes about 5000 ticker with 900 fields starting from January 1998. It uses the <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic14015.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open FineFundamental API Documentation">FineFundamental </a> type. </p> 
          <p> For the <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic14015.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open FineFundamental API Documentation">FineFundamental </a> properties, please checkout our <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/data#fundamentals/usa/morningstar">database</a>. </p> 
          <p> Like coarse universes, fine universes allow you to select an unlimited universe of symbols to analyse. You are only limited by practical memory and speed limits and may quickly run out of memory if you backtest too many symbols in parallel. These limits can be increased with a subscription. Also you must use coarse fundamental universe to narrow down the universe as a "pre-filter". </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">// Take the top 50 by dollar volume using coarse
// Then the top 10 by PERatio using fine
AddUniverse(
    coarse =&gt; {
        return (from c in coarse
            where c.Price &gt; 10
            orderby c.DollarVolume descending
            select c.Symbol).Take(50);
    },
    fine =&gt; {
        return (from f in fine
            orderby f.ValuationRatios.PERatio descending
            select f.Symbol).Take(10);
    });</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python"># In Initialize:
self.AddUniverse(self.CoarseSelectionFunction, self.FineSelectionFunction)

def CoarseSelectionFunction(self, coarse):
    '''Take the top 50 by dollar volume using coarse'''
    # sort descending by daily dollar volume
    sortedByDollarVolume = sorted(coarse, \
        key=lambda x: x.DollarVolume, reverse=True) 

    # we need to return only the symbol objects
    return [ x.Symbol for x in sortedByDollarVolume[:50] ]

def FineSelectionFunction(self, fine):
    '''sort the data by P/E ratio and take the top 10 '''
    # sort descending by P/E ratio
    sortedByPeRatio = sorted(fine, \
        key=lambda x: x.ValuationRatios.PERatio, reverse=True)

    # take the top entries from our sorted collection
    return [ x.Symbol for x in sortedByPeRatio[:10] ]</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Universes-Custom-Universe-Selection"> Custom Universe Selection <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/10 Universes/05 Custom Universe Selection" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Universes-Custom-Universe-Selection" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <p> Custom universes allow using an external data source as the security filtering source. Like normal custom data sources, custom universes are provided by extending BaseData. With this system you can define data formats to filter and select the data. </p> 
          <p> Each <code>BaseData</code> of the custom universe is 1 line of the source file. The Reader method will be called repeatedly until the date/time advances or the end of file is reached. This way you the engine can group universe data together, and pass it as a single collection into the filter function. </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python"># In Initialize
self.AddUniverse(NyseTopGainers, "myCustomUniverse", Resolution.Daily, self.nyseTopGainers)

def nyseTopGainers(self, data):
    return [ x.Symbol for x in data if x["Rank"] &gt; 5 ]</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python"># Example custom universe data; it is virtually identical to other custom data types.
class NyseTopGainers(PythonData):

    def GetSource(self, config, date, isLiveMode):
        return SubscriptionDataSource(@"your-remote-universe-data", SubscriptionTransportMedium.RemoteFile)
    
    def Reader(self, config, line, date, isLiveMode):
        # Generate required data, then return an instance of your class.
        nyse = NyseTopGainers()
        nyse.Time = date
        # define end time as exactly 1 day after Time
        nyse.EndTime = nyse.Time + timedelta(1)
        nyse.Symbol = Symbol.Create(symbolString, SecurityType.Equity, Market.USA)
        nyse["Rank"] = rank
        return nyse</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Universes-Option-Universes"> Option Universes <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/10 Universes/06 Option Universes" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Universes-Option-Universes" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <p> When you add an option to the algorithm it adds many many individual option contract securities. These are modelled as a "universe" of option contracts. We provide the <code>SetFilter</code> method to help narrow the option strike and expiry dates down to a range you are interested. </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style="border-bottom: 1px solid #eee; "> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Universes-Future-Universes"> Future Universes <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/10 Universes/07 Future Universes" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Universes-Future-Universes" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section"> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12"> 
         <h2 id="Historical-Data"> Historical Data <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/11 Historical Data" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true" style="font-size:0.7em;"></i> </a> <a href="#Historical-Data" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h2> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container"></div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Historical-Data-Introduction-to-Historical-Data"> Introduction to Historical Data <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/11 Historical Data/01 Introduction to Historical Data" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Historical-Data-Introduction-to-Historical-Data" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <p> Historical data can be provided in a batch request, or by "warming up" your algorithm. Batch requests feed requested data back as an enumerable you can use to manually prime your algorithm. The warm up feature feeds data to your event handlers from before your start date for a fixed period. </p> 
          <p> In live mode the history API can return data up to 5 seconds before the present moment. </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Historical-Data-Historical-Data-Requests"> Historical Data Requests <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/11 Historical Data/02 Historical Data Requests" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Historical-Data-Historical-Data-Requests" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <p> Batch history API is often easier to understand as you can manually feed data into your components which need it. If Resolution of the data request is not specified the history API uses the resolution of data you've specified with AddSecurity() or your Universe. If the Symbol is not specified then history for all symbols is returned for the period. </p> 
          <p class="csharp"> Batch data returned as <code>IEnumerable&lt;Slice&gt; slices</code>, <code>IEnumerable&lt;TradeBar&gt; slices</code> or <code>IEnumerable&lt;QuoteBar&gt; slices</code> has all the normal slice helpers - to assist using the data in your strategy, for example: </p> 
          <pre class="csharp">
//From slice -&gt; tradebars, or slice -&gt; decimals.
IEnumerable&lt;Slice&gt; slices = History(TimeSpan.FromDays(7), Resolution.Minute);
IEnumerable&lt;TradeBar&gt; bars = slices.Get("SPY"); // Bars 
IEnumerable&lt;decimal&gt; decimals = slices.Get("SPY", Field.Close); // Close from slice
// Many math libraries need double arrays, decimals -&gt; double[]
double[] doubleArray = decimals.ToDoubleArray();
</pre> 
          <p class="python"> In Python batch data can also be returned as pandas.DataFrame. It is a multi-index dataframe where the first index is the symbol. </p> 
          <pre>
slices = self.History(["SPY","EURUSD"], 14)
bars = slices.loc["EURUSD"]
doubleArray = bars["close"]   # use lowercase
</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">// Request history for specific symbol, default to AddSecurity resolution.
IEnumerable&lt;TradeBar&gt; bars = History("SPY", TimeSpan.FromDays(7));
// Request history for specific symbol, at specific resolution.
IEnumerable&lt;TradeBar&gt; bars = History("SPY", TimeSpan.FromDays(7), Resolution.Minute);

//Get last 14 bars of SPY, default to AddSecurity resolution.
//Note you can't get "14 ticks" -- getting a specific number of bars only applies to TradeBar data.
IEnumerable&lt;TradeBar&gt; bars = History("SPY", 14);
//Get last 14 bars of SPY, at specific resolution.
IEnumerable&lt;TradeBar&gt; bars = History("SPY", 14, Resolution.Minute);

// Request history for specific symbol, default to AddSecurity resolution.
IEnumerable&lt;QuoteBar&gt; bars = History&lt;QuoteBar&gt;("EURUSD", TimeSpan.FromDays(7));
// Request history for specific symbol, at specific resolution.
IEnumerable&lt;QuoteBar&gt; bars = History&lt;QuoteBar&gt;("EURUSD", TimeSpan.FromDays(7), Resolution.Minute);

//Get last 14 bars of EURUSD, default to AddSecurity resolution.
//Note you can't get "14 ticks" -- getting a specific number of bars only applies to QuoteBar data.
IEnumerable&lt;QuoteBar&gt; bars = History&lt;QuoteBar&gt;("EURUSD", 14);
//Get last 14 bars of EURUSD, at specific resolution.
IEnumerable&lt;QuoteBar&gt; bars = History&lt;QuoteBar&gt;("EURUSD", 14, Resolution.Minute);

// Get history for all tickers we're subscribed to, at their native resolution
IEnumerable&lt;Slice&gt; slices = History(TimeSpan.FromDays(7));
// Get history for all tickers we're subscribed to, at a specific resolution
IEnumerable&lt;Slice&gt; slices = History(TimeSpan.FromDays(7), Resolution.Minute);

// For custom data, we need to define the type. E.g.: Quandl
AddData&lt;Quandl&gt;("SYMBOL")
IEnumerable&lt;Quandl&gt; bars = History&lt;Quandl&gt;("SYMBOL", TimeSpan.FromDays(7));
IEnumerable&lt;Quandl&gt; bars = History&lt;Quandl&gt;("SYMBOL", 14);
</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python"># Get history for all tickers we're subscribed to, at their native resolution
slices = self.History(timedelta(7))
# Get history for all tickers we're subscribed to, at a specific resolution
slices = self.History(timedelta(7), Resolution.Minute)

# Equity case:
# Request history for specific symbol, default to AddSecurity resolution.
bars = self.History("SPY", TimeSpan.FromDays(7))
# Request history for specific symbol, at specific resolution.
bars = self.History("SPY", TimeSpan.FromDays(7), Resolution.Minute)

# Get last 14 bars of SPY, default to AddSecurity resolution.
# Note you can't get "14 ticks" -- getting a specific number of bars only applies to TradeBar data.
bars = self.History("SPY", 14)
# Get last 14 bars of SPY, at specific resolution.
bars = self.History("SPY", 14, Resolution.Minute)

# Other assets (QuoteBar) case:
# We need to use map method to select only the specific symbol
bars = map(lambda x: x["EURUSD"], self.History(timedelta(7)))
bars = map(lambda x: x["EURUSD"], self.History(timedelta(7), Resolution.Minute))
bars = map(lambda x: x["EURUSD"], self.History(14))
bars = map(lambda x: x["EURUSD"], self.History(14, Resolution.Minute))

# Get history in pandas.DataFrame format, use list of string
df = self.History(["EURUSD"], timedelta(7))
df = self.History(["EURUSD"], timedelta(7), Resolution.Minute)
df = self.History(["EURUSD"], 14)
df = self.History(["EURUSD"], 14, Resolution.Minute)</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style="border-bottom: 1px solid #eee; "> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Historical-Data-Warming-Your-Algorithm"> Warming Your Algorithm <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/11 Historical Data/03 Warming Your Algorithm" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Historical-Data-Warming-Your-Algorithm" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <p> Warming up your algorithm causes data from before the algorithm starts to be fed into the conventional data event handlers. This system of warm up lends itself to stream style algorithms. </p> 
          <p> The data flowing to your algorithm will seamlessly pass from historical to live data. The flag <code>bool IsWarmingUp</code> can be used to monitor this transition. </p> 
          <p> During the warm up period you cannot submit orders. Warm up also does not support universe selection while the algorithm is warming up. </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">SetWarmUp(200); //Warm up 200 bars for all subscribed data.
SetWarmUp(TimeSpan.FromDays(7)); //Warm up 7 days of data.</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python">self.SetWarmUp(200) //Warm up 200 bars for all subscribed data.
self.SetWarmUp(timedelta(7)) //Warm up 7 days of data.</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section"> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12"> 
         <h2 id="Reality-Modelling"> Reality Modelling <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/12 Reality Modelling" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true" style="font-size:0.7em;"></i> </a> <a href="#Reality-Modelling" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h2> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container"></div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Reality-Modelling-Introduction-to-Models"> Introduction to Models <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/12 Reality Modelling/01 Introduction to Models" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Reality-Modelling-Introduction-to-Models" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <p> Models can be used to improve the accuracy of your backtesting. We provide basic default models which assume you are trading on highly liquid assets, but if you are trading high volumes, or on low volume assets you should update these models to be more realistic. </p> 
          <p> All models are set on a per security basis. To set a model first fetch the security object and apply your model. </p>
          <pre>//Set IBM to have a constant $1 transaction fee. 
Securities["IBM"].FeeModel = new ConstantFeeTransactionModel(1); </pre> 
          <p></p> 
          <p> All models should be setup in your Initialize() method. </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Reality-Modelling-Brokerage-Models"> Brokerage Models <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/12 Reality Modelling/02 Brokerage Models" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Reality-Modelling-Brokerage-Models" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <p> We provide a shortcut to set common models and properties relating to each of the brokerages we support. These brokerage models set fees, fill models, slippage models and trading markets for a brokerage. In addition they validate it is possible to submit trades to the brokerage (e.g. submitting equity trades to a forex only brokerage). </p>
          <ul> 
           <li> Transaction fees models </li> 
           <li> Supported markets </li> 
           <li> Slippage model </li> 
           <li> Validate orders and updates before they are submitted </li> 
           <li> Default account type (margin or cash account) </li> 
           <li> Support for extended market hours </li> 
           <li> How splits and dividends are applied to open order tickets </li> 
           <li> Default leverage for assets </li> 
           <li> Default settlement models </li> 
          </ul> This gives you enormous control over your algorithm behavior and allow you to model virtually any brokerage in the world. 
          <p></p> 
          <p> In addition to our default brokerage model ( <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic7875.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open DefaultBrokerageModel API Documentation">DefaultBrokerageModel </a> ), we provide brokerage models for Interactive Brokers ( <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic7915.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open InteractiveBrokersBrokerageModel API Documentation">InteractiveBrokersBrokerageModel </a> ) , FXCM ( <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic7894.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open FxcmBrokerageModel API Documentation">FxcmBrokerageModel </a> ), OANDA ( <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic7925.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open OandaBrokerageModel API Documentation">OandaBrokerageModel </a> ) and Tradier ( <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic7946.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open TradierBrokerageModel API Documentation">TradierBrokerageModel </a> ). </p> 
          <p> Brokerage models override any other models you may set for a security. </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">// Set brokerage model using helper methods:
SetBrokerageModel(BrokerageName.FxcmBrokerage); // Defaults to margin account
SetBrokerageModel(BrokerageName.TradierBrokerage, AccountType.Cash); //Or override account type

// Supported brokerage names:
BrokerageName.FxcmBrokerage
             .OandaBrokerage
             .TradierBrokerage
             .InteractiveBrokersBrokerage</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">// You can also create your own brokerage model: IBrokerageModel
class MyBrokerage: DefaultBrokerage {
   // Custom implementation of brokerage here.
} 

SetBrokerageModel(new MyBrokerage());</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python"># Set brokerage model using helper methods:
self.SetBrokerageModel(BrokerageName.FxcmBrokerage) # Defaults to margin account
self.SetBrokerageModel(BrokerageName.TradierBrokerage, \ 
                       AccountType.Cash) # Or override account type

# Supported brokerage names:
BrokerageName.FxcmBrokerage
             .OandaBrokerage
             .TradierBrokerage
             .InteractiveBrokersBrokerage</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Reality-Modelling-Transaction-Fee-Models"> Transaction Fee Models <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/12 Reality Modelling/03 Transaction Fee Models" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Reality-Modelling-Transaction-Fee-Models" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <p> Transaction fee models set the fees for each order. We provide customized transaction models for all brokerages, but you can also set your own. Like all models they must be set on a security by security basis. </p> 
          <p> Transaction models implement the <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic26551.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open ISecurityTransactionModel API Documentation">ISecurityTransactionModel </a> interface. If you wish to implement your own transaction model you can start with the <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic26220.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open SecurityTransactionModel API Documentation">SecurityTransactionModel </a> and override methods you wish to change. </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">// Set IBM to use a fixed $1.5 per trade fee model.
Securities["IBM"].FeeModel = new ConstantFeeTransactionModel(1.5);

// Set EURUSD to use FXCM's transaction fees:
Securities["EURUSD"].FeeModel = new FxcmTransactionModel();</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python"># Set IBM to use a fixed $1.5 per trade fee model.
self.Securities["IBM"].FeeModel = ConstantFeeTransactionModel(1.5)

# Set EURUSD to use FXCM's transaction fees:
self.Securities["EURUSD"].FeeModel = new FxcmTransactionModel()</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">// Assigning securities custom fee models:
Securities["SPY"].SetFeeModel(new CustomFeeModel());

// Custom fee implementation
public class CustomFeeModel : IFeeModel {
    public decimal GetOrderFee(Security security, Order order) {
        return 1;
    }
}</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python"># Assigning securities custom fee models:
self.Securities["SPY"].SetFeeModel(CustomFeeModel()) 

# Custom fee implementation
class CustomFeeModel:
    def GetOrderFee(self, security, order):
        return 1</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Reality-Modelling-Slippage-Models"> Slippage Models <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/12 Reality Modelling/04 Slippage Models" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Reality-Modelling-Slippage-Models" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <p> Slippage is the difference in price between your last reported quote and the real price the trade filled at. This difference can be positive or negative, as sometimes the price can slip in your favor. In volatile markets you are likely to experience more slippage. </p> 
          <p> Slippage models implement the <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic24724.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open ISlippageModel API Documentation">ISlippageModel </a> interface. We provide the <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open SpreadSlippageModel API Documentation">SpreadSlippageModel </a> for forex based securities, and the <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic24730.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open ConstantSlippageModel API Documentation">ConstantSlippageModel </a> for Equities. </p> 
          <p> Advanced users may wish to implement their own volatility based slippage model - increasing the accuracy of your backtests in volatile markets. </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">// Assigning securities custom slippage models:
Securities["SPY"].SetSlippageModel(new CustomSlippageModel());

// Custom slippage implementation
public class CustomSlippageModel : ISlippageModel {
    public decimal GetSlippageApproximation(Security asset, Order order) {
        return 0.1m;
    }
}</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python"># Assigning securities custom slippage models:
self.Securities["SPY"].SetSlippageModel(CustomSlippageModel())

# Custom slippage implementation
class CustomSlippageModel:
    def GetSlippageApproximation(self, asset, order):
        return 0.1</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Reality-Modelling-Fill-Models"> Fill Models <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/12 Reality Modelling/05 Fill Models" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Reality-Modelling-Fill-Models" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <p> Fill models give you control over order fills. Each supported order type is passed through a dedicated method and returns an <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic24450.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open OrderEvent API Documentation">OrderEvent </a> object. OrderEvents are used to carry information about order partial fills or errors. </p> 
          <p> The Fill Models implement the <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic24668.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open IFillModel API Documentation">IFillModel </a> interface. They have the following key methods:</p>
          <pre>public interface IFillModel {
    OrderEvent MarketFill(Security asset, MarketOrder order);
    OrderEvent StopMarketFill(Security asset, StopMarketOrder order);
    OrderEvent StopLimitFill(Security asset, StopLimitOrder order);
    OrderEvent LimitFill(Security asset, LimitOrder order);
    OrderEvent MarketOnOpenFill(Security asset, MarketOnOpenOrder order);
    OrderEvent MarketOnCloseFill(Security asset, MarketOnCloseOrder order);
}</pre>We provide the 
          <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic24679.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open ImmediateFillModel API Documentation">ImmediateFillModel </a> which assumes orders and immediately and completely filled. 
          <p></p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">// Set the fill models in initialize:
Securities["IBM"].SetFillModel(new PartialFillModel());

// Custom fill model implementation stub
public class PartialFillModel : ImmediateFillModel {
    public override OrderEvent MarketFill(Security asset, MarketOrder order) {
        //Override order event handler and return partial order fills, 
    }
}</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python"># Set the fill models in initialize:
self.Securities["IBM"].SetFillModel(PartialFillModel())

# Custom fill model implementation stub
class PartialFillModel(ImmediateFillModel):
    def MarketFill(self, asset, order):
        # Override order event handler and return partial order fills
        pass</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Reality-Modelling-Margin-Models"> Margin Models <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/12 Reality Modelling/06 Margin Models" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Reality-Modelling-Margin-Models" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <p> Margin models control how much buying power your algorithm has to make trades. Margin calculations can be very complex and depends on many factors including the brokerage or even time of day. </p> 
          <p> Margin model implement the <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic25329.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open ISecurityMarginModel API Documentation">ISecurityMarginModel </a> interface and default to the <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic26092.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open SecurityMarginModel API Documentation">SecurityMarginModel </a> class. We also provide the <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic25833.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open PatternDayTradingMarginModel API Documentation">PatternDayTradingMarginModel </a> to model intraday pattern day trading for US equities. </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">// Example of setting a security to use PDT margin models:
// Generally you do not need to adjust margin models
Securities["AAPL"].MarginModel = new PatternDayTradingMarginModel();</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python"># Example of setting a security to use PDT margin models:
# Generally you do not need to adjust margin models
self.Securities["AAPL"].MarginModel =  PatternDayTradingMarginModel()</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Reality-Modelling-Settlement-Models"> Settlement Models <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/12 Reality Modelling/07 Settlement Models" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Reality-Modelling-Settlement-Models" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <p> After a trade is made brokerages settle the cash depending on the markets and account type. This is managed by our Settlement Models. The most common settlement type is immediate - where the funds are available for trading immediately. This is handled by the <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic25676.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open ImmediateSettlementModel API Documentation">ImmediateSettlementModel </a> . US Equities trading with cash accounts is typically settled 3 days after the transaction occurred. This is managed by the <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic25475.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open DelayedSettlementModel API Documentation">DelayedSettlementModel </a> . </p> 
          <p> Settlement models implement the <a href="https://www.quantconnect.com/lean/docs#topic25359.html" target="_BLANK" class="lean-documentation" title="Open ISettlementModel API Documentation">ISettlementModel </a> interface. You can create your own settlement model by implementing this method. Most users will not need to create their own settlement model and can use one of the ones provided above. </p> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-example-container section-fill"> 
         <div class="section-example csharp"> 
          <pre class="csharp">// Set a security to a delayed settlement model: settle 7 days later, at 8am.
Securities["IBM"].SettlementModel = new DelayedSettlementModel(7, new TimeSpan(8, 0, 0));</pre> 
         </div> 
         <div class="section-example python"> 
          <pre class="python"># Set a security to a delayed settlement model: settle 7 days later, at 8am.
self.Securities["IBM"].SettlementModel =  DelayedSettlementModel(7, timedelta(hours = 8))</pre> 
         </div> 
        </div> 
        <div class="section-background"></div> 
       </div> 
       <div class="row section" style=""> 
        <div class="col-lg-6 col-md-6 col-sm-12 section-copy-container"> 
         <div class="section-copy"> 
          <h3 id="Reality-Modelling-Portfolio-Models"> Portfolio Models <a href="https://github.com/QuantConnect/Documentation/tree/master/02 Algorithm Reference/12 Reality Modelling/08 Portfolio Models" class="anchor-link" target="_blank"> <i class="fa fa-github" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> <a href="#Reality-Modelling-Portfolio-Models" class="anchor-link"> <i class="fa fa-anchor" aria-hidden="true"></i> </a> </h3> 
          <p> Portfolio models control how order fills are applied to your portfolio.
